.ui_button--FlatStyle--blue:hover{background-color:rgba(0,0,0,0.02)}</style><div id='__w2_wbeZGQ6S33_answer_content'><div id='wbeZGQ6S37'><div class='inline_editor_content' id='__w2_wbeZGQ6S38_content'><span class='inline_editor_value' id='__w2_wbeZGQ6S38_answer_content'><div id='__w2_wbeZGQ6S43_expanded_content'><div id='wbeZGQ6S45'></div><div class='TranslatedAnswerBanner'></div><div class='u-serif-font-main--large'><div class='ui_qtext_expanded'><span class="ui_qtext_rendered_qtext"><blockquote><p class="ui_qtext_para">I will assume you are asking this question as a beginner, and try answering accordingly. I too am a beginner, so I&#039;m actually following most of the things I&#039;ve described here.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>Preparation Strategy</b></p><p class="ui_qtext_para">Google kickstart heavily focuses on proficiency in <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/data-structures/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Data Structures</a></span> and <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/fundamentals-of-algorithms/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Algorithms</a></span> and to prepare for it is not an easy task but sure an enjoyable one. This article is written assuming that the reader has a mild experience in programming because only then he/she is aiming for a career.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>Brushing up the basics:</b> Solve various easy-medium level problems so you grasp the important small tips and tweaks. This will also increase your efficiency, accuracy and speed.</p><ul><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://code.google.com/codejam/kickstart/contests.html" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="google.com">Practice previous Contest Problems at CodeJam</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://practice.geeksforgeeks.org/Easy/0/0/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Practice at GeeksforGeeks</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.codechef.com/problems/easy/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="codechef.com">Practice at Codechef</a></span></li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para">Solving many problems from here will build up your base</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>What to study?</b></p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>a) Learn</b> <b>Number Theory</b></p><ul><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://practice.geeksforgeeks.org/topics/number%20theory/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Practice Number Theory Problems</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://artofproblemsolving.com/community/c90633h1291397" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="artofproblemsolving.com">Learn art of Problem Solving</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="/What-important-topics-of-number-theory-should-every-programmer-know">Important topics of number theory – Quora</a></span></li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>b) Greedy algorithms: </b>Although questions from greedy are seldom asked but are important as they lay foundation for various algorithms. Refer <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/category/algorithm/greedy/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">this</a></span> to find greedy algorithm problems.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>c) Binary Search:</b> Is a very important tool when it comes to problem solving and problems based on it are asked repetitively. Good articles to be read:</p><ul><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.topcoder.com/community/data-science/data-science-tutorials/binary-search/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="topcoder.com">Binary Search – TopCoder</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/tag/binary-search/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Binary Search – GeeksforGeeks</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/the-ubiquitous-binary-search-set-1/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">The Ubiquitous Binary Search</a></span></li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>d) Graphs:</b> Google kickstart is an easy-medium test hence basic-medium level questions from the graphs can be asked. Do practice questions based on: DFS, BFS, Dijkstra, Flloyd Warshall, MST and flow problems.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>e) Dynamic programming:</b> Although variety of questions can be designed from the DP domain but fairly easy to medium questions are predicted. Practice DP a lot and do read:</p><ul><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/category/algorithm/dynamic-programming/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Dynamic Programming – GeeksforGeeks</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.codechef.com/wiki/tutorial-dynamic-programming" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="codechef.com">Dynamic Programming – Codechef</a></span></li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>f)Divide and Conquer : </b>This topic also helps solving problems in KickStart.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>g) More Advance Topics:</b><br />Though problems from advanced data structures are seldom asked do read about Trie, BIT tree, BST. Also read:-</p><ul><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/hashing-data-structure/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Hashing</a></span></li><li><span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/bitwise-algorithms/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Bit Algorithms</a></span></li><li>String Algorithms (<span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/searching-for-patterns-set-3-rabin-karp-algorithm/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Rabin Karp</a></span>, <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/searching-for-patterns-set-2-kmp-algorithm/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">KMP</a></span>, <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/aho-corasick-algorithm-pattern-searching/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199886);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Aho-Crosaick</a></span>)</li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>Pointers</b></p><ol><li>Google Kickstart is all about speed and accuracy, focus on your speed rather than solving very tough problems and solve easy-medium problems as much as you can.</li><li>Get familiar with Big-O notation and calculation of computation time.</li><li>Start preparing beforehand and don’t lose hope if you don’t perform well in a round, there are 5 more rounds after the first round.</li><li>Excellent Performance can get you a call from Google for interview.</li><li>Aim to get within 100 in first few APAC tests (A, B or C) . It will brighten your chances for interview shortlisting.</li></ol><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>With that said, I would like to highlight a few points which have been helpful to me:</b></p><ul><li>Try solving as many problems as possible. The more you practice, the faster and better you get.</li><li>DO NOT give up on a problem. Spend at least a couple of hours on a given problem. If you don&#039;t succeed , take a break and come back again and try solving it later. Keep thinking about the problem, most likely you&#039;ll stumble upon an idea. Once you get the key idea, coding it won&#039;t be too hard.</li><li>Try solving at least one problem every week. If you don&#039;t do this, you&#039;ll get slower as more time passes.</li><li>After solving the problem on your own, try going through other solutions. They are sometimes much more efficient and understanding them might be beneficial to you later.</li><li>Register on the <span class="qlink_container"><a href="/topic/USA-Computing-Olympiad-USACO">USA Computing Olympiad (USACO)</a></span> Training Gateway, and try completing the course. (I&#039;m currently doing this)</li><li>After getting comfortable with problems, participate in monthly contests on websites like Codechef. They are fun, and might help to keep you interested.</li><li>You could sign up for an Algorithms course on Coursera , which might prove helpful not only for this , but also your course work if you happen to study Computer Science.</li><li>Final advice, this one is really important. Don&#039;t get intimidated by a contest and decide on &quot;participating later&quot;. I had that thought in mind, but I decided to give Code Jam a try and I actually succeeded. So don&#039;t be shy to try. Even if you fail, you can keep on trying the problems and later , if required, view the solutions.</li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para">All the best!!</p><hr class="qtext_hr" /><p class="ui_qtext_para"><i>Spoiler Alert regarding Big-O notation - Time Complexity of various data sets:</i></p><p class="ui_qtext_para">O(1) - Blink an eye<br />O(n^2) - Grab a coffee<br />O(n^4) - Take a Nap<br />O(3^n) - Go for a walk<br />O(n!) - Take a vacation<br />O(n^n) - Quit your programming job</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b><i>~SMR²</i></b></p></blockquote></span></div></div><div             <path d="M7.73218309,9.96973049 C6.28500703,10.4895228 5.25,11.873892 5.25,13.5 L12.75,13.5 C12.75,11.873892 11.714993,10.4895228 10.2678169,9.96973049 C11.2910047,9.49195022 12,8.45377247 12,7.25 C12,5.59314575 10.6568542,4.25 9,4.25 C7.34314575,4.25 6,5.59314575 6,7.25 C6,8.45377247 6.70899528,9.49195022 7.73218309,9.96973049 Z M17.25,11.3388626 C16.9783814,11.4955 16.7318899,11.7061926 16.5273952,11.9688404 L14.7662908,14.2307581 C13.7898614,13.2559226 12.2080519,13.2564142 11.232233,14.232233 C10.4142783,15.0501878 10.2816074,16.2939234 10.8342204,17.25 L4.5,17.25 C2.42893219,17.25 0.75,15.5710678 0.75,13.5 L0.75,4.5 C0.75,2.42893219 2.42893219,0.75 4.5,0.75 L13.5,0.75 C15.5710678,0.75 17.25,2.42893219 17.25,4.5 L17.25,11.3388626 Z" class="icon_svg-fill_as_stroke" fill="#666" fill-rule="nonzero"></path>

    </g>
</svg></span></div><span class='ui_button_count hidden' aria-hidden='true' id='__w2_wVf9Mq7K16_count_wrapper'><span class='ui_button_count_optimistic_counts' id='__w2_wVf9Mq7K16_count'><span class='ui_button_count_optimistic_count'>0</span><span class='ui_button_count_optimistic_count'>1</span></span></span></div></div></a></span></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div id='__w2_wVwUV8KH9_answer_content'><div id='wVwUV8KH13'><div class='inline_editor_content' id='__w2_wVwUV8KH14_content'><span class='inline_editor_value' id='__w2_wVwUV8KH14_answer_content'><div id='__w2_wVwUV8KH19_expanded_content'><div id='wVwUV8KH21'></div><div class='TranslatedAnswerBanner'></div><div class='u-serif-font-main--large'><div class='ui_qtext_expanded'><span class="ui_qtext_rendered_qtext"><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>Getting familiar with the Judging Environment</b></p><ul><li>You can use any programming language or IDE if they are licensed.</li><li>Judging environment is quite different, instead of just uploading your code, you need to upload an output text file also.</li><li>Competition arena consists of problems to be solved.</li><li>For any single problem there exist 2 subparts</li><li>Small Input with small constraints.</li><li>Large Input with large constraints.</li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para">When you have coded the problem and want to submit it for small inputs, download the text file, as soon as the file is downloaded a timer of 4 min starts and you have to run your inputs over your code and upload the text file within the time limit.<br />&nbsp;You will immediately get to know if your submission was correct .<br />&nbsp;In case of more than 1 submissions, the submission which fetched the most points first (small or large) will be considered and a penalty will be awarded for wrong submissions. Each time you download the file, a new set of test file is generated.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para">Submitting for large inputs, a timer of 8 minutes start and you have to submit your code and output file along with it within the time limit but in this case the output file will remain the same in contrast to the small inputs.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para">To get acquainted with the environment, please refer this <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://code.google.com/codejam/resources/quickstart-guide" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199867);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="google.com">QuickStart guide</a></span> .</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b>Preparation Strategy</b></p><p class="ui_qtext_para">Google Code Jam heavily focuses on proficiency in <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/data-structures/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199867);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Data Structures</a></span> and <span class="qlink_container"><a href="https://www.geeksforgeeks.org/fundamentals-of-algorithms/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199867);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="geeksforgeeks.org">Algorithms</a></span> and to prepare for it is not an easy task but sure an enjoyable one. This article is written assuming that the reader has a mild experience in programming because only then he/she is aiming for a career.</p><ol><li><b><i>Try solving as many problems as possible. The more you practice, the faster and better you .</i></b></li><li><b><i>NOT give up on a problem. Spend at least a couple of hours on a given problem. If you don&#039;t succeed , take a break and come back again and try solving it later. Keep thinking about the problem, most likely you&#039;ll stumble upon an idea. Once you get the key idea, coding it won&#039;t be too hard.</i></b></li><li><b><i>Try solving at least one problem every week. If you don&#039;t do this, you&#039;ll get slower as more time passes.</i></b></li><li><b><i>After solving the problem on your own, try going through other solutions. They are sometimes much more efficient and understanding them might be beneficial to you later.</i></b></li><li><b><i>Register on the </i></b><span class="qlink_container"><a href="/topic/USA-Computing-Olympiad-USACO"><b><i>USA Computing Olympiad (USACO)</i></b></a></span><b><i> Training Gateway, and try completing the course. (I&#039;m currently doing this)</i></b></li><li><b><i>After getting comfortable with problems, participate in monthly contests on websites like Codechef. They are fun, and might help to keep you interested.</i></b></li><li><b><i>You could sign up for an Algorithms course on Coursera , which might prove helpful not only for this , but also your course work if you happen to study Computer Science. Final advice, this one is really important. Don&#039;t get intimidated by a contest and decide on &quot;participating later&quot;. I had that thought in mind, but I decided to give Code Jam a try and I actually succeeded. So don&#039;t be shy to try. Even if you fail, you can keep on trying the problems and later , if required, view the solutions.</i></b></li></ol><p class="ui_qtext_para"><i>Here are some resources that might prove helpful</i>:</p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b><i>Codechef </i></b>: <span class="qlink_container"><a href="http://www.codechef.com/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199867);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="codechef.com">Programming Competition,Programming Contest,Online Computer Programming</a></span></p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b><i>USACO Training Pages</i></b> : <span class="qlink_container"><a href="http://cerberus.delos.com:790/usacogate" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199867);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="delos.com">Page on Delos</a></span></p><p class="ui_qtext_para"><b><i>Topcoder</i></b> : <span class="qlink_container"><a href="http://www.topcoder.com/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199867);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="topcoder.com">TopCoder, Inc. | Home of the world&#039;s largest development community.</a></span><br /><b><i>Stackoverflow</i></b>(for any programming doubts) : <span class="qlink_container"><a href="http://stackoverflow.com/" rel="noopener nofollow" target="_blank" onclick="return Q.openUrl(this, 68199867);" class="external_link" data-qt-tooltip="stackoverflow.com">Stack Overflow</a></span></p></span></div></div><div     </g>
</svg></span></div><span class='ui_button_count hidden' aria-hidden='true' id='__w2_wlgAJRvN71_count_wrapper'><span class='ui_button_count_optimistic_counts' id='__w2_wlgAJRvN71_count'><span class='ui_button_count_optimistic_count'>0</span><span class='ui_button_count_optimistic_count'>1</span></span></span></div></div></a></span></div></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div id='__w2_wlgAJRvN9_answer_content'><div id='wlgAJRvN13'><div class='inline_editor_content' id='__w2_wlgAJRvN14_content'><span class='inline_editor_value' id='__w2_wlgAJRvN14_answer_content'><div id='__w2_wlgAJRvN19_expanded_content'><div id='wlgAJRvN21'></div><div class='TranslatedAnswerBanner'></div><div class='u-serif-font-main--large'><div class='ui_qtext_expanded'><span class="ui_qtext_rendered_qtext"><p class="ui_qtext_para">Google Code jam is not just about solving problems barely with knowledge, one can struggle solving a problem even if the algorithm is known.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para">Its a competition of application of knowledge at its best, one needs to be smart and it <i>wont</i> come by just reading, implementing and understanding algorithms. You will have to make those algorithms yours, as if you have made them, see a problem, lets say <i>insertion sorting</i>, think what can be done to solve it by squeezing the time complexity.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para">Once you have a approach, code it and analyze its complexity. Check if its time complexity is as good as the algorithm, if it is, compare the approaches, if its not try again, if you don’t end up with one that is as good as established complexity, refer the solution, think from the perspective of the creator of algorithm at each step, why did he think of this approach?</p><p class="ui_qtext_para">Ignite the research element.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para">Once you will be able to question the approach of an algorithm, and find answers to your own question, you will love it. After this stage you will be able to approach a problem with a positive insight and design and analyze the algorithm for the same.</p><p class="ui_qtext_para">That being said, we should now come to points that would help particularly for GCJ :</p><ul><li>Past problems are the key, you need to solve them and once done go through the <b>contest analysis</b>.</li><li>Introduction to Algorithms - CLRS will help you achieve the stage that we talked about earlier.</li><li>Time is a crucial factor after qualification round, you need to appear in other contests (hackerrank, codechef, topcoder, whatever you think is right for you) before the GCJ round 1.</li></ul><p class="ui_qtext_para">The most important thing is implementing this, bridging the knowledge-action gap is the key, I knew all this way back when I failed in GCJ 2017 round 1 itself.</p></span></div></div><div id='wlgAJRvN25'><div class='ContentFooter AnswerFooter' id='__w2_wlgAJRvN26_content_footer'><span
